# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Grafana Alerting Rule Evaluation to Notification Chain

## Your Task

Trace how a Grafana unified alerting rule is evaluated and fired in grafana/grafana. Find Go source files implementing: the rule scheduler, the rule evaluation, the alert state transition, and the alert notification dispatch to receivers.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/grafana--26d36ec` (grafana/grafana)
- `sg-evals/grafana-loki` (grafana/loki)
- `sg-evals/grafana-mimir` (grafana/mimir)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

70-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've created a comprehensive trace of how Grafana unified alerting rules are evaluated and fired. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I traced the complete flow of a Grafana unified alerting rule from scheduling through notification dispatch:

### Core Components:

1. **Rule Scheduler** (`schedule/schedule.go`): Orchestrates periodic evaluation of all alert rules using a ticker-based system
   
2. **Alert Rule Evaluator** (`schedule/alert_rule.go`): Each rule runs in its own goroutine, receives evaluation signals, and manages retry logic

3. **Evaluation Engine** (`eval/eval.go`): Executes rule queries/expressions using the expression service to produce metric results

4. **State Manager** (`state/manager.go`): Processes evaluation results, determines state transitions, and decides which alerts to send based on thresholds and timing

5. **Alerts Router** (`sender/router.go`): Routes alerts to internal Alertmanager and/or external Alertmanagers based on organization configuration

6. **Multi-Org Alertmanager** (`notifier/multiorg_alertmanager.go`): Maintains per-organization Alertmanager instances for isolation

7. **Internal Alertmanager** (`notifier/alertmanager.go`): Receives alerts and dispatches them through the notification routing engine to receivers/integrations

### Complete Flow:
Scheduler → Rule Evaluation → Query Execution → State Calculation → Alert Decision → Router → Org Alertmanager → Receivers

The answer file includes all relevant files, key symbols, the complete call chain, and detailed narrative documentation at `/workspace/answer.json`.

Overview\\nGrafana's unified alerting system (ngalert) evaluates alert rules on a schedule and dispatches fired alerts through notification receivers. The flow consists of four main components: rule scheduling, rule evaluation, state management, and notification dispatch.\\n\\n### Rule Scheduler\\n**File:** `pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/schedule.go`\\n\\nThe scheduler is the entry point that orchestrates periodic evaluation of alert rules. Key functions:\\n- `Run(ctx context.Context)`: Starts the scheduler, initializes a ticker, and enters the main evaluation loop\\n- `schedulePeriodic(ctx context.Context, t *ticker.T)`: Main loop that:\\n  - Tracks which alert rules are scheduled for evaluation\\n  - Fetches alert rules from the rules store periodically\\n  - Sends evaluation signals to individual alert rule routines\\n  - Handles rule additions, deletions, and updates\\n  - Uses retry configuration for resilience\\n\\nThe scheduler maintains a rule registry where each alert rule has its own dedicated goroutine for execution.\\n\\n### Alert Rule Evaluation\\n**File:** `pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/alert_rule.go`\\n\\nEach alert rule runs in its own goroutine orchestrated by the `alertRule` struct. Key functions:\\n\\n- `newAlertRule()`: Factory function that creates an alert rule with state manager, evaluator factory, and sender dependencies\\n\\n- `Run()`: Main loop for an individual alert rule that:\\n  - Receives evaluation signals via a channel (`evalCh`)\\n  - Receives update signals to change rule configuration (`updateCh`)\\n  - Handles rule state resets when updated or paused\\n  - Implements exponential backoff retry logic\\n  - Delegates to `evaluate()` for actual evaluation\\n\\n- `Eval(eval *Evaluation)`: Signals the rule to perform evaluation by sending to `evalCh`\\n\\n- `evaluate(ctx, e *Evaluation, span, shouldRetry, logger)`: Core evaluation logic that:\\n  - Creates a new evaluator from the factory for the rule's condition\\n  - Calls `ruleEval.Evaluate()` to execute queries/expressions\\n  - Measures evaluation duration and tracks metrics\\n  - Calls `stateManager.ProcessEvalResults()` with evaluation results and a callback to send alerts\\n  - Implements retry logic with exponential backoff\\n\\n- `send(ctx, logger, states StateTransitions)`: Converts state transitions to PostableAlerts and calls `sender.Send()`\\n\\n- `expireAndSend(ctx, states)`: Sends resolved alerts when rules are deleted or updated\\n\\n### Evaluation Engine\\n**File:** `pkg/services/ngalert/eval/eval.go`\\n\\nThe evaluator executes the rule's query/expression condition. Key components:\\n\\n- `EvaluatorFactory`: Interface with `Create()` method that builds evaluators for rule conditions\\n\\n- `NewEvaluatorFactory()`: Creates the evaluator factory, configured with evaluation timeout and result limits\\n\\n- `ConditionEvaluator`: Interface with:\\n  - `Evaluate(ctx, now time.Time)`: Evaluates condition and returns typed Results\\n  - `EvaluateRaw(ctx, now time.Time)`: Returns raw backend response\\n\\n- `EvaluateAlert()`: Converts backend query response to alert instance states (determined by alert values, thresholds, and evaluation time)\\n\\n### State Management and Transitions\\n**File:** `pkg/services/ngalert/state/manager.go`\\n\\nManages alert instance state and determines which alerts to send to notification receivers:\\n\\n- `Manager`: Core state management component that:\\n  - Caches alert instance states per rule\\n  - Persists state to database\\n  - Coordinates with historian for audit trail\\n\\n- `ProcessEvalResults(ctx, evaluatedAt time.Time, alertRule, results, extraLabels, send Sender)`: Main method that:\\n  - Calls `setNextStateForRule()` to compute state transitions based on evaluation results\\n  - Handles NoData and Error states based on rule configuration\\n  - Processes missing series (firing alerts with no data in current evaluation)\\n  - Calls `updateLastSentAt()` to determine which states should be sent\\n  - Persists all state changes (both sent and unsent)\\n  - Records state transitions in historian\\n  - Invokes the `send` callback with state transitions to send\\n\\n- `setNextStateForRule()`: Determines new states for each alert instance based on:\\n  - Evaluation results and thresholds\\n  - Previous state of the alert instance\\n  - Pending duration (time alert must breach threshold before firing)\\n  - NoDataState and ExecutionErrorState rule configuration\\n\\n- `updateLastSentAt()`: Filters state transitions to identify which should be sent based on:\\n  - State changes (e.g., firing to normal)\\n  - Resend delay (30 seconds by default)\\n  - Resolved alert retention period\\n\\n- `DeleteStateByRuleUID()`: Removes all instances of a rule and creates resolved state transitions for firing alerts\\n\\n### Alert Notification Dispatch\\n**File:** `pkg/services/ngalert/sender/router.go`\\n\\nRoutes alerts to internal and/or external Alertmanagers:\\n\\n- `AlertsRouter`: Handles alert routing based on organization configuration. Key functions:\\n  - `NewAlertsRouter()`: Creates router with dependencies on multi-org alertmanager and external alertmanager configuration\\n  - `Send(ctx, key AlertRuleKey, alerts PostableAlerts)`: Main dispatch function that:\\n    - Checks if organization is configured for internal, external, or both alertmanagers\\n    - Gets org's alertmanager from `multiOrgNotifier.AlertmanagerFor()`\\n    - Calls `PutAlerts()` on the alertmanager\\n    - Sends to external alertmanagers if configured via `ExternalAlertmanager.SendAlerts()`\\n    - Broadcasts alerts to cluster peers if enabled\\n  - `SyncAndApplyConfigFromDatabase()`: Periodically syncs alertmanager configuration from database\\n  - Maintains list of external alertmanagers per organization\\n\\n### Multi-Org Alertmanager\\n**File:** `pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/multiorg_alertmanager.go`\\n\\nManages separate Alertmanager instances per Grafana organization:\\n\\n- `MultiOrgAlertmanager`: Container for organization-specific alertmanagers. Key functions:\\n  - `NewMultiOrgAlertmanager()`: Factory that:\\n    - Sets up clustering if configured (Redis for HA)\\n    - Initializes per-org alertmanager factory\\n    - Configures alert broadcast channel for cluster communication\\n  - `AlertmanagerFor(orgID)`: Returns or creates alertmanager for given organization\\n  - Creates per-org Alertmanager instances on demand with isolation\\n\\n### Internal Alertmanager (Per-Organization)\\n**File:** `pkg/services/ngalert/notifier/alertmanager.go`\\n\\nHandles notification delivery and routing for a single organization:\\n\\n- `alertmanager`: Wraps the core `GrafanaAlertmanager` from the alerting library. Key functions:\\n  - `NewAlertmanager()`: Creates org-specific alertmanager that:\\n    - Initializes state stores for silences and notification logs\\n    - Sets up maintenance options for periodic garbage collection\\n    - Loads persisted silence and notification log state\\n    - Configures dispatch timer (async or sync)\\n  - `PutAlerts(ctx, postableAlerts)`: Receives alerts and:\\n    - Converts Grafana alert models to alerting library models\\n    - Calls `Base.PutAlerts()` on the wrapped `GrafanaAlertmanager`\\n    - This sends alerts through the Alertmanager's dispatch pipeline to receivers/integrations\\n\\n### Service Integration\\n**File:** `pkg/services/ngalert/ngalert.go`\\n\\nWires up all components:\\n- Creates and initializes the scheduler\\n- Creates state manager with persistence layer\\n- Creates evaluator factory\\n- Creates alerts router\\n- Creates multi-org alertmanager\\n- Coordinates lifecycle of all services\\n\\n### Complete Call Chain\\n\\n1. **Scheduler Start**: `schedule.Run()` \u2192 `schedulePeriodic()`\\n2. **Rule Evaluation Signal**: Scheduler sends eval signal to alert rule's channel\\n3. **Rule Processing**: `alertRule.Run()` receives signal \u2192 calls `Eval()`\\n4. **Evaluation Execution**: `evaluate()` \u2192 `evalFactory.Create()` \u2192 `ConditionEvaluator.Evaluate()` \u2192 `EvaluateAlert()`\\n5. **State Processing**: `stateManager.ProcessEvalResults()` \u2192 `setNextStateForRule()` \u2192 `updateLastSentAt()`\\n6. **Alert Dispatch**: Callback invokes `alertRule.send()` \u2192 `AlertsRouter.Send()`\\n7. **Routing to Alertmanager**: `AlertsRouter.Send()` \u2192 `MultiOrgAlertmanager.AlertmanagerFor()` \u2192 org's `Alertmanager.PutAlerts()`\\n8. **Notification Delivery**: `Alertmanager.PutAlerts()` \u2192 `GrafanaAlertmanager.PutAlerts()` \u2192 dispatcher sends to receivers/integrations\\n\\nThis modular architecture allows for:\\n- Per-organization isolation via MultiOrgAlertmanager\\n- Flexible routing (internal/external alertmanagers)\\n- Proper state tracking and notification deduplication\\n- Resilience with retry logic and state persistence\\n- Clustering support for high availability\"\n}\n",
